The Generosity of Celestial Causes and the Futility of Du'a
Argues that if celestial causes are generous, their refusal before du'a indicates intrinsic impossibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the ninth argument, which uses the generosity of high causes to argue that du'a cannot change their predetermined actions.

Core Idea
If celestial causes are generous, their refusal before du'a proves they cannot grant it.

This passage presents the ninth argument against the efficacy of supplication. The opponent claims that the celestial causes are inherently generous and merciful. If they could grant a request, they would do so immediately, without waiting for a prayer. Since they do not, the request must be impossible—either because the cause cannot produce it (essential impossibility) or because it would harm the world's welfare. Let's examine the reasoning closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Notice the concise argumentative style.
The key terms are 'high causes' (العلل العالية), 'miserliness' (بخل), 'generosity' (جود), and 'essential impossibility' (امتناع ذاتي).
2
Identify the two premises
Identify the two premises: (1) the high causes are free from miserliness and described by generosity. (2) They give mercy. From these, the conclusion is drawn that their refraining before supplication indicates impossibility.
The word 'فامتناعها' connects the generosity to the refraining.
3
Understand the two alternatives for impossibility
The passage gives two reasons for the impossibility: either essential impossibility (the cause cannot produce the effect by its nature) or because the effect is contrary to the world's benefit (maslaha). Note that both alternatives make du'a ineffective.
Essential impossibility means it's not within the cause's power; beneficial impossibility means giving it would disrupt cosmic order.
4
Reflect on the theological flaw
Consider the common misunderstanding: the argument assumes the high causes are real agents independent of God. From an Islamic perspective, the true agent is Allah alone, and du'a is a commanded act that can lead to divine decree. This argument mistakenly presupposes a self-sufficient causal system.
The common misunderstanding is taken from the source chunk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة : إن العلل العالية منزهة عن البخل ، موصوفة بالجود ، وإفادة الرحمة فامتناعها عن ذلك (١) قبل الدعاء ، يدل على امتناعها في أنفسها . إما بحسب الامتناع الذاتي ، أو لأجل أنها على ضد المصلحة الملائمة (٣) للعالم .
The ninth proof: The high causes are free from miserliness, described by generosity and giving mercy. So their refraining from that action before supplication indicates their impossibility in themselves – either according to essential impossibility, or because they are contrary to the suitable benefit for the world.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage presents the ninth argument based on the attributes of the high causes (al-`ilal al-`aliya). These causes are inherently generous and not miserly. If they were able to grant the requested benefit, they would have done so before any du'a, out of their innate generosity. Since they do not grant it, this shows that granting it is either essentially impossible for them (essential impossibility) or it would conflict with what is beneficial for the world (maslaha). Therefore, du'a cannot change their action, and so it is pointless.

Key Terms
علل عالية
بخل
جود
امتناع ذاتي
مصلحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The high causes are real, independent agents that can act without God's will.
Correction: Islamic theology holds that Allah alone is the true Creator and Agent; all causes are contingent and subservient to His will.

Checkpoint
According to the ninth argument, why do the high causes not grant the requested thing before du'a?
A) Because they are miserly.
B) Because they are unaware.
C) Because it is either essentially impossible or against the world's benefit.
D) Because they wait for the supplication.

Key Takeaway
The ninth argument claims that the generosity of high causes renders du'a futile because refusal implies essential or beneficial impossibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When your du'a seems delayed or unanswered, do you ever feel that what you ask for is simply impossible? How does this lesson’s reminder that only Allah can bring the impossible into existence change how you wait for His response?
?
This argument says that a generous cause would give without being asked. When you pray, do you sometimes act as if you need to convince Allah to give? How can you instead approach du'a as an act of worship that pleases Him regardless of the outcome?
?
The lesson mentions that what is not given may be because it is against the 'suitable benefit for the world.' Think of a du'a you made that was not fulfilled. Can you see, even in hindsight, that perhaps not receiving it was better for you or others? What does that tell you about Allah's wisdom and your trust in His plan?

The Supplicant's State as a Condition for Divine Effects
The author argues that the supplicant's focused state during prayer may be a necessary condition for the flow of effects from higher causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the supplicant's focused state during prayer is considered a necessary temporal condition for the flow of effects from higher causes, and how this deepens the understanding of prayer's efficacy.

Core Idea
The supplicant's state is as crucial as the agent's state for the desired effect to occur.

This lesson unpacks a subtle but profound principle: the effectiveness of prayer depends not only on Allah's will but also on the state of the supplicant. The author uses the causal framework of agent and recipient to argue that the soul's condition during prayer may be a necessary temporal condition for divine action. We will explore how this understanding elevates the role of focused worship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how the author builds from a general principle to a specific application.
Pay attention to the logical connectors like 'لا شك أنه' and 'إذن'.
2
Identify the general principle
Find the author's statement that both the agent's state and the recipient's state matter for producing an effect. Also note the point about temporal conditions.
The author uses 'كذلك' to parallel the two.
3
Apply to prayer
See how the author applies the principle: the supplicant's soul conditioned during prayer may be a temporal condition for the outflow of effects from high causes.
Contrast with the idea that effects would be perpetual without conditions.
4
Explore the deeper dimension
Understand the second part: when fully absorbed, a light from the unseen and an effect from dominating spirits appear, strengthening the soul and enabling the desired event.
This adds a spiritual empowerment aspect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفائدة الثانية : لا شك أنه كما يعتبر في حصول الأثر ، حال الفاعل ، فكذلك يعتبر حال القابل. وأيضاً : فتأثيرات تلك العلل العالية في حوادث هذا العالم ، لا شك أنها موقوفة على شرائط حادثة ، وإلا لـدامت الآثار لدوام تلك المؤثرات . إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : إنه لا يمتنع أن يكون تكيف نفس الداعي بالكيفية الحاصلة عند الدعاء كان شرطاً لفيضان تلك الآثار عن تلك العلل العالية ، فعند حصول هذه الحالة، تحدث تلك الآثار عن تلك العلل العالية ولا يمتنع أيضاً أن يقال : إن نفس الداعي عند الاستغراق في الدعاء ، يظهر فيها نور من أنوار عالم الغيب ، وأثر من آثار تلك الأرواح القاهرة . وحينئذ تقوی جوهر النفس البشرية ، ويحصل لها استعلاء في تلك الحالة ، وبواسطة تلك القوة [ والقدرة (۳) ] يحصل ذلك الحادث المطلوب
The second benefit: There is no doubt that just as the state of the agent is considered in the occurrence of the effect, so too is the state of the recipient considered. Also, the effects of those high causes upon the events of this world are undoubtedly dependent upon temporal conditions; otherwise the effects would persist as long as those effectors persist. When you know this, we say: It is not impossible that the conditioning of the supplicant's soul with the quality obtained at the time of prayer be a condition for the outflow of those effects from those high causes. So when this state occurs, those effects occur from the high causes. And it is not impossible also to say that when the supplicant's soul is absorbed in prayer, there appears in it a light from the lights of the unseen world and an effect from the effects of those dominating spirits. Then the substance of the human soul becomes strong, and it gains a supremacy in that state, and by means of that power [and capability] that desired event occurs.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage presents the second benefit of prayer. It begins with a general principle: both the agent's state and the recipient's state are relevant for producing an effect. The effects of higher causes on worldly events are dependent on temporal conditions; otherwise they would be perpetual. The author then applies this to prayer: the supplicant's soul, conditioned by the quality attained during prayer, may be a temporal condition for the outflow of effects from those high causes. When this state occurs, the effects follow. Furthermore, when the supplicant's soul is absorbed in prayer, a light from the unseen world and an effect from dominating spirits appear in it, strengthening the soul and granting it supremacy, through which the desired event is realized.

Key Terms
الفاعل
القابل
العلل العالية
الشروط الحادثة
الأرواح القاهرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prayer's effectiveness is solely dependent on God's will, regardless of the supplicant's state.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the supplicant's focused state is a necessary temporal condition for the outflow of effects from higher causes; thus, the recipient's state plays a crucial role.

Checkpoint

A) The higher causes are weak
B) The supplicant lacks sincerity
C) They depend on temporal conditions, including the supplicant's state
D) The higher causes change their minds

Key Takeaway
The supplicant's focused state during prayer is a temporal condition that, along with divine illumination, enables the outflow of effects from higher causes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
This lesson says the supplicant's soul must be conditioned. Is your soul conditioned for divine reception, or are you expecting effects from high causes while your heart is distracted? What one distraction will you remove today to prepare your soul?

This reconnection empowers the soul to affect the material world in extraordinary ways. The passage invites us to see prayer not just as worship but as a cosmic re-linking.

The Recipient's Condition in Supplication
Al-Razi explains that the efficacy of supplication depends on the state of the supplicant's soul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the effectiveness of supplication depends on the spiritual state of the supplicant, as explained by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi through a causal framework.

Core Idea
Supplication works when the soul is properly conditioned to receive divine influence.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi addresses a subtle point about supplication: its efficacy is not automatic but depends on the state of the one who prays. By drawing an analogy to causality in the natural world, he shows that the supplicant's soul must be in a receptive state. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and its implications for understanding how supplication operates.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its literal translation to grasp the full argument. Notice the flow from general principle to specific application.
The passage is a second benefit (fa'ida) in a larger discussion.
2
Understand the causal analogy
Al-Razi starts by equating the state of the agent and the state of the recipient in producing an effect. Recognize that both are necessary conditions.
This is a foundational principle in Islamic cosmology.
3
Identify the condition for supplication
The key point: the supplicant's soul must be in a specific state (achieved through supplication) for the high causes to bring about the effect. This state is a condition, not the cause itself.
4
Examine the strengthening of the soul
Al-Razi adds that absorption in supplication brings light from the unseen and strengthens the soul, enabling the desired event. Note the spiritual dimension.
This connects to the concept of spiritual power.
5
Reflect on the lesson's implication
Ask yourself how this understanding changes your view of supplication. Does it make supplication more intentional and spiritually demanding?
Consider the common misconception that supplication is always effective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفائدة الثانية : لا شك أنه كما يعتبر في حصول الأثر حال الفاعل فكذلك يعتبر حال القابل. وأيضاً فتأثيرات تلك العلل العالية في حوادث هذا العالم لا شك أنها موقوفة على شرائط حادثة وإلا لدامت الآثار لدوام تلك المؤثرات. إذا عرفت هذا فنقول إنه لا يمتنع أن يكون تكيف نفس الداعي بالكيفية الحاصلة عند الدعاء كان شرطاً لفيضان تلك الآثار عن تلك العلل العالية فعند حصول هذه الحالة تحدث تلك الآثار عن تلك العلل العالية ولا يمتنع أيضاً أن يقال إن نفس الداعي عند الاستغراق في الدعاء يظهر فيها نور من أنوار عالم الغيب وأثر من آثار تلك الأرواح القاهرة. وحينئذ تقوى جوهر النفس البشرية ويحصل لها استعلاء في تلك الحالة وبواسطة تلك القوة والقدرة يحصل ذلك الحادث المطلوب.
The second benefit: There is no doubt that just as the state of the agent is considered in the occurrence of the effect, so also the state of the recipient is considered. Also, the influences of those high causes upon the events of this world are undoubtedly dependent on contingent conditions, otherwise the effects would persist due to the persistence of those influences. If you understand this, we say: It is not impossible that the conditioning of the supplicant's soul with the state that occurs at the time of supplication is a condition for the emanation of those effects from those high causes. So when this state occurs, those effects arise from those high causes. And it is also not impossible to say that the supplicant himself, when absorbed in supplication, a light from the lights of the Unseen world appears in him, and an effect from the effects of those powerful spirits. Then the substance of the human soul becomes strong, and it gains ascendancy in that state, and by means of that strength and power, that desired event occurs.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a second benefit (fa'ida) explaining the conditions for the efficacy of supplication (du'a). The author, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, establishes a parallel between the state of the agent and the state of the recipient in producing an effect. He argues that the influences of high celestial causes on worldly events are contingent upon temporary conditions; otherwise, effects would be perpetual. Applying this to supplication, he states that the soul of the supplicant must be in a specific state—achieved through the act of supplication—as a condition for the emanation of effects from those causes. When this state is attained, the effects occur. Moreover, during absorption in supplication, the supplicant receives a light from the Unseen and an influence from powerful spirits, which strengthens the human soul and grants it ascendancy, enabling the desired event to come about. The passage emphasizes that receptivity and proper conditioning are crucial for supplication to be effective.

Key Terms

القابل (al-qābil)
العلل العالية (al-‘ilal al-‘āliya)
الدعاء (al-du‘ā’)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that supplication is always effective regardless of the spiritual state of the supplicant.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that the supplicant's soul must be in a specific receptive state for supplication to be effective.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Supplication is effective only when the supplicant's soul is in the right state to receive divine influence.

The Soul's Link to Celestial Spirits
Al-Razi describes the soul's connection to a celestial spirit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's concept of the soul's connection to a celestial spirit and how purification and supplication lead to spiritual power.

Core Idea
Each human soul is connected to a celestial spirit; purification attracts that spirit's power.

Al-Razi begins this benefit by reminding us of a foundational idea: every human soul has a corresponding celestial spirit that serves as its origin and source. This relationship, he explains, is like that of a child to a father or a slave to a master. Through purification and concentrated supplication, the soul can reconnect with that spirit and gain extraordinary abilities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core relationship
Read the passage carefully to understand how Al-Razi describes the relationship between the human soul and the celestial spirit.
Note the similes: like children to a father, slaves to a master.
2
Understand the process of purification and attraction
Trace the steps: the soul undertakes purification, then persists in supplication, leading to attraction to the celestial spirit.
3
Recognize the resulting effects
Notice that through this connection, the soul gains power over the lower world, resulting in wondrous effects.
This sets the stage for the discussion on communal worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفائدة الثالثة : إنا قد ذكرنا أن لكل واحدة من هذه النفوس البشرية روحاً من الأرواح العالية الفلكية وتكون هذه النفوس البشرية بالنسبة إلى تلك الروح كالأولاد بالنسبة إلى الأب وكالعبيد بالنسبة إلى المولى فإذا أخذت النفس في التصفية عن العلائق الجسدانية ثم بالغت في الدعاء والتضرع انجذبت هذه النفوس إلى تلك الروح الفلكي الذي هو الأصل والمعدن والمنبع وبسبب ذلك الانجذاب والاتصال يحصل في جوهر هذه النفس البشرية قوة وقدرة وسلاطة على هيولى العالم الأسفل فحينئذ تحصل آثار عجيبة وأحوال غريبة. إذا عرفت هذا فنقول اجتماع الجمع العظيم على الدعاء الواحد في المقصود الواحد أقوى تأثيراً من إقدام الشخص الواحد على ذلك العمل لأن عند الاجتماع تنضم المؤثرات الكثيرة بعضها إلى البعض فيكون التأثير أقوى لا محالة وقد ضرب العلماء لهذا مثالاً فقالوا القرانات مرتبة على أربع مراتب : القرآن الأصغر والأوسط والأكبر والأعظم. والسبب في هذا التفاوت أنه كلما كانت الكواكب أكثر وكان قرب بعضها من البعض أتم كان التأثير أقوى. فلهذا السبب أمرت الشريعة الحقة بترتيب الاجتماعات على أربع مراتب فأولها أداء الصلوات الخمس في الجماعات لأن القوم إذا اجتمعوا حصلت من تلك الجمعية آثار لا تحصل عند الانفراد وثانيها صلاة الجمعة في الأسبوع فإن الجمعية هناك أكثر وأتم مما في غيرها فلا جرم تكون قوتها أكمل وأفضل وثالثها صلاة العيد فالجمعية فيها أتم وأكمل وأكثر مما في صلاة الجمعة ورابعها وهو القرآن الأعظم اجتماع العالم في موقف الحج فإن الجمع العظيم من أهل المشرق والمغرب يجتمعون في ذلك الموقف ويوجهون أفكارهم وأذهانهم إلى استنزال الرحمة وطلب المعونة من الله تعالى فلا جرم يحصل فيه من التأثير ما لا يحصل من سائر الوجوه ولهذا الباب شرائط كثيرة سنذكرها في شرح السحر المبني على الأوهام وتصفية النفوس فهذا ما يمكن شرحه باللسان ومن خاض في هذا الطريق وجد فيه من أنواع الفوائد ما لا يمكن ذكره باللسان ولا شرحه بالأقلام والهادي إلى الحق ليس إلا الملك العلام.
The third benefit: We have mentioned that each of these human souls has a spirit from the high celestial spirits, and these human souls are in relation to that spirit like children in relation to the father, and like slaves in relation to the master. So when the soul undertakes purification from bodily attachments, then persists in supplication and humility, these souls are attracted to that celestial spirit, which is the origin, source, and fountainhead. And due to that attraction and connection, strength, power, and dominion over the matter of the lower world occur in the substance of this human soul. Then wondrous effects and strange states occur. If you understand this, we say: The gathering of a great multitude for a single supplication for a single purpose is more powerful than the action of a single person for that task, because at the gathering, many influences are combined together, so the influence is necessarily stronger. The scholars have given an example for this: They said that gatherings are arranged in four ranks: the smallest gathering, the medium, the greater, and the greatest. The reason for this variation is that the more numerous the planets [or congregations] and the more complete their proximity to one another, the stronger the influence. For this reason, the true Law (shari'a) has ordered the arrangement of gatherings in four ranks: First: performing the five daily prayers in congregation, because when people gather, effects result from that gathering that do not occur when alone. Second: the Friday prayer every week, for the gathering there is more numerous and more complete than in others; hence its strength is more perfect and superior. Third: the Eid prayer; the gathering there is more complete and more numerous than the Friday prayer. Fourth, which is the greatest gathering: the gathering of the world (all people) at the station of Hajj. For the great multitude from East and West gather at that station and direct their thoughts and minds to seeking mercy and requesting assistance from God Almighty. Hence there results from it an influence that does not result from other ways. This chapter has many conditions that we will mention in the explanation of magic based on illusions and the purification of souls. This is what can be explained by the tongue. Whoever plunges into this path finds in it types of benefits that cannot be mentioned by the tongue nor explained by pens. And the Guide to truth is none other than the King, the All-Knowing.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage presents the third benefit, which builds on the idea of the soul's connection to higher celestial spirits. Al-Razi explains that each human soul has a corresponding celestial spirit as its origin, forming a filial and servile relationship. Through purification and earnest supplication, the soul is attracted to this spirit, acquiring strength and dominion over the material world, resulting in extraordinary effects. He then applies this understanding to communal worship: a large group unified in purpose and supplication combines their spiritual influences, producing a stronger effect than an individual. He cites the scholars' analogy of planetary conjunctions (qirānāt), which are arranged in four ascending ranks based on the number and proximity of the planets—analogous to congregations. Accordingly, the true Law (shari'a) has instituted four levels of communal worship: (1) daily congregational prayers, (2) Friday prayer, (3) Eid prayer, and (4) the Hajj assembly, each increasing in gathering size and spiritual power. Al-Razi notes that further conditions for this chapter will be discussed in his explanation of 'magic based on illusions' and purification of souls. He concludes by stating that these benefits are experiential and beyond full verbal description, and that God alone is the Guide to truth.

النفوس البشرية (al-nufūs al-bashariyya)
الروح الفلكي (al-rūḥ al-falakī)
التصفية (al-tasfiya)
الدعاء (al-du‘ā')
الانجذاب (al-injidhāb)

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Four Ranks of Congregational Worship
Al-Razi enumerates the four ranks of congregational worship and their basis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why congregational worship is more powerful than individual worship and how Islamic law organizes it into four ascending ranks based on the analogy of planetary conjunctions.

Core Idea
The power of worship increases with the size and unity of the congregation, mirroring planetary conjunctions.

After explaining the soul's connection to celestial spirits, Al-Razi applies this principle to communal worship. He argues that when a large group unites for a single purpose, their combined spiritual influences produce a stronger effect. Citing the scholars' analogy of planetary conjunctions, he shows that Islamic law has instituted four ranks of congregational worship, each more powerful than the last.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of combined influence
Read the opening statement: a great multitude united in supplication is more powerful than a single person.
The reasoning: many influences combine to produce a stronger effect.
2
Grasp the analogy of planetary conjunctions
The scholars compare gatherings to planetary conjunctions; more planets and closer proximity yield stronger influence.
This analogy explains why larger, more unified gatherings are more powerful.
3
Identify the four ranks of congregational worship
List the four ranks as given: daily prayers, Friday prayer, Eid prayer, and Hajj.
Notice the increasing size and unity at each level.
4
Reflect on the culminating rank of Hajj
The Hajj assembly is the greatest, with people from East and West, resulting in the strongest influence.
Al-Razi emphasizes that the full benefits are experiential and beyond description.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفائدة الثالثة : إنا قد ذكرنا أن لكل واحدة من هذه النفوس البشرية روحاً من الأرواح العالية الفلكية وتكون هذه النفوس البشرية بالنسبة إلى تلك الروح كالأولاد بالنسبة إلى الأب وكالعبيد بالنسبة إلى المولى فإذا أخذت النفس في التصفية عن العلائق الجسدانية ثم بالغت في الدعاء والتضرع انجذبت هذه النفوس إلى تلك الروح الفلكي الذي هو الأصل والمعدن والمنبع وبسبب ذلك الانجذاب والاتصال يحصل في جوهر هذه النفس البشرية قوة وقدرة وسلاطة على هيولى العالم الأسفل فحينئذ تحصل آثار عجيبة وأحوال غريبة. إذا عرفت هذا فنقول اجتماع الجمع العظيم على الدعاء الواحد في المقصود الواحد أقوى تأثيراً من إقدام الشخص الواحد على ذلك العمل لأن عند الاجتماع تنضم المؤثرات الكثيرة بعضها إلى البعض فيكون التأثير أقوى لا محالة وقد ضرب العلماء لهذا مثالاً فقالوا القرانات مرتبة على أربع مراتب : القرآن الأصغر والأوسط والأكبر والأعظم. والسبب في هذا التفاوت أنه كلما كانت الكواكب أكثر وكان قرب بعضها من البعض أتم كان التأثير أقوى. فلهذا السبب أمرت الشريعة الحقة بترتيب الاجتماعات على أربع مراتب فأولها أداء الصلوات الخمس في الجماعات لأن القوم إذا اجتمعوا حصلت من تلك الجمعية آثار لا تحصل عند الانفراد وثانيها صلاة الجمعة في الأسبوع فإن الجمعية هناك أكثر وأتم مما في غيرها فلا جرم تكون قوتها أكمل وأفضل وثالثها صلاة العيد فالجمعية فيها أتم وأكمل وأكثر مما في صلاة الجمعة ورابعها وهو القرآن الأعظم اجتماع العالم في موقف الحج فإن الجمع العظيم من أهل المشرق والمغرب يجتمعون في ذلك الموقف ويوجهون أفكارهم وأذهانهم إلى استنزال الرحمة وطلب المعونة من الله تعالى فلا جرم يحصل فيه من التأثير ما لا يحصل من سائر الوجوه ولهذا الباب شرائط كثيرة سنذكرها في شرح السحر المبني على الأوهام وتصفية النفوس فهذا ما يمكن شرحه باللسان ومن خاض في هذا الطريق وجد فيه من أنواع الفوائد ما لا يمكن ذكره باللسان ولا شرحه بالأقلام والهادي إلى الحق ليس إلا الملك العلام.
The third benefit: We have mentioned that each of these human souls has a spirit from the high celestial spirits, and these human souls are in relation to that spirit like children in relation to the father, and like slaves in relation to the master. So when the soul undertakes purification from bodily attachments, then persists in supplication and humility, these souls are attracted to that celestial spirit, which is the origin, source, and fountainhead. And due to that attraction and connection, strength, power, and dominion over the matter of the lower world occur in the substance of this human soul. Then wondrous effects and strange states occur. If you understand this, we say: The gathering of a great multitude for a single supplication for a single purpose is more powerful than the action of a single person for that task, because at the gathering, many influences are combined together, so the influence is necessarily stronger. The scholars have given an example for this: They said that gatherings are arranged in four ranks: the smallest gathering, the medium, the greater, and the greatest. The reason for this variation is that the more numerous the planets [or congregations] and the more complete their proximity to one another, the stronger the influence. For this reason, the true Law (shari'a) has ordered the arrangement of gatherings in four ranks: First: performing the five daily prayers in congregation, because when people gather, effects result from that gathering that do not occur when alone. Second: the Friday prayer every week, for the gathering there is more numerous and more complete than in others; hence its strength is more perfect and superior. Third: the Eid prayer; the gathering there is more complete and more numerous than the Friday prayer. Fourth, which is the greatest gathering: the gathering of the world (all people) at the station of Hajj. For the great multitude from East and West gather at that station and direct their thoughts and minds to seeking mercy and requesting assistance from God Almighty. Hence there results from it an influence that does not result from other ways. This chapter has many conditions that we will mention in the explanation of magic based on illusions and the purification of souls. This is what can be explained by the tongue. Whoever plunges into this path finds in it types of benefits that cannot be mentioned by the tongue nor explained by pens. And the Guide to truth is none other than the King, the All-Knowing.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage presents the third benefit, which builds on the idea of the soul's connection to higher celestial spirits. Al-Razi explains that each human soul has a corresponding celestial spirit as its origin, forming a filial and servile relationship. Through purification and earnest supplication, the soul is attracted to this spirit, acquiring strength and dominion over the material world, resulting in extraordinary effects. He then applies this understanding to communal worship: a large group unified in purpose and supplication combines their spiritual influences, producing a stronger effect than an individual. He cites the scholars' analogy of planetary conjunctions (qirānāt), which are arranged in four ascending ranks based on the number and proximity of the planets—analogous to congregations. Accordingly, the true Law (shari'a) has instituted four levels of communal worship: (1) daily congregational prayers, (2) Friday prayer, (3) Eid prayer, and (4) the Hajj assembly, each increasing in gathering size and spiritual power. Al-Razi notes that further conditions for this chapter will be discussed in his explanation of 'magic based on illusions' and purification of souls. He concludes by stating that these benefits are experiential and beyond full verbal description, and that God alone is the Guide to truth.

Key Terms
القرانات (al-qirānāt)
الجماعة (al-jamā‘a)
الصلوات الخمس (al-ṣalawāt al-khams)
الجمعة (al-jum‘a)
العيد (al-‘īd)
الحج (al-ḥajj)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Individual supplication is always equivalent in power to communal supplication.
Correction: Al-Razi explains that communal supplication combines multiple influences, resulting in a stronger effect.

Checkpoint
According to the third benefit, what is the reason for the four ranks of congregational worship in Islamic law?
A) They are based on the number of planets in conjunction at the time.
B) They are based on the increasing number and proximity of participants, which strengthens the spiritual influence.
C) They are arbitrarily assigned by jurists without any underlying principle.
D) They are meant to test the obedience of the community.

Key Takeaway
Congregational worship is more powerful than individual worship, and Islamic law organizes it into four ranks, culminating in Hajj.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray alone, do you truly believe that joining the congregation would make your prayer more powerful? If you hold back, what fear or laziness is stronger than your desire for that power? Will you commit to attending at least one congregational prayer today, not out of habit, but to test this principle?
?
You have attended Friday prayers and Eids—but have you ever gone with the conscious intention of combining your supplication with others for a single purpose? What if you did? What would change in your heart? This Friday, resolve to focus on the unity of the congregation's plea before you even enter the mosque.
?
Al-Razi says that those who plunge into this path find benefits beyond description. Are you merely reading about spiritual power, or are you plunging? What is one step you can take this week—beyond your current routine—to experience the combined influence of the community, perhaps by organizing a small group du‘a’ gathering or by making sincere intentions for Hajj?

Causality and Created Things
beginner
5 min
Human Ability to Devise Wondrous Crafts
Defines the second human faculty: inventiveness, its components, and contrast with animals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic theological view of human inventiveness, its two components (imagination and body), and how it differs from animal behavior driven by divine inspiration.

Core Idea
Human invention stems from rational derivation; animal crafts arise from divine inspiration, not reason.

In this passage, the author identifies the second unique human characteristic: the ability to invent wondrous crafts. He breaks this faculty into its principle (imagination) and instrument (body), and contrasts it with apparently similar animal behaviors like bees building hexagonal combs. The distinction lies in human reasoning versus divinely inspired instinct. This lesson unpacks that distinction and its theological implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its English translation. Notice the structure: definition, components, animal comparison, and a note on refutation.
2
Identify the two components
Find the terms for principle (مبدأ) and instrument (آلة) and their definitions. The principle is imagination (خيال); the instrument is the body (بدن).
Aristotle's term 'permitted instrument' is noted but not central.
3
Contrast with animal behavior
Consider the bee example: why does the author say it is not real invention? Because it lacks derivation (استنباط) and analogy (قياس); it is pure inspiration (إلهام).
This guards against the misconception that animals share human-like creativity.
4
Note the refutation
The author hints that the Shaykh's claim about animal uniformity is refuted by celestial motion, and promises a later chapter. This shows the dialectical nature of the work.
We won't resolve the refutation here; just observe its presence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثاني من خواص الإنسان : قدرته على استنباط الصنائع العجيبة ولهذه القدرة مبدأ وآلة أما المبدأ فهو الخيال القادر على تركيب الصور بعضها بالبعض وأما الآلة فهي البدن وقد سماها الحكيم أرسطاطاليس الآلة المباحة وسنذكر تفسير هذه اللفظة في علم التشريح إن شاء الله وقد يحصل ما يشبه هذه الحالة للحيوانات الأخس كالنحل في بناء البيوت المسدسة إلا أن ذلك لا يُصدر عن استنباط وقياس بل عن إلهام وتسخير ولذلك لا تختلف ولا تتنوع هكذا قاله الشيخ وهو منقوض بالحركة الفلكية وسنفرد لهذا البحث فصلاً على الاستقصاء
The second type of human characteristics: his ability to derive wondrous crafts. This ability has a principle and an instrument. As for the principle, it is the imagination capable of composing forms with one another. As for the instrument, it is the body. The philosopher Aristotle called it 'the permitted instrument'. We will mention the explanation of this term in the science of anatomy, God willing. And sometimes a situation similar to this occurs in lower animals, like bees in building hexagonal houses, except that this does not originate from derivation and analogy, but from inspiration and subjugation; therefore they do not differ or vary. Thus said the Shaykh. But it is refuted by the celestial motion. We will devote a chapter to this investigation exhaustively.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage identifies the second type of human characteristics: the ability to invent wondrous crafts. It states that this ability has two components: a principle, which is the imagination that can combine forms, and an instrument, which is the body. Aristotle called the body 'the permitted instrument'. The author notes that similar behaviors occur in lower animals like bees building hexagonal combs, but these are not due to derivation or reasoning; they are by divine inspiration and subjugation, hence they are uniform and unchanging. The author then notes that this position of the Shaykh is refuted by the motion of the celestial spheres, and he promises to discuss this in detail in a separate chapter.

Key Terms
استنباط
الصنائع العجيبة
الخيال
البدن
الآلة المباحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That animal craftsmanship (e.g., bee hives) is the same as human inventiveness because both produce complex structures.
Correction: The passage clarifies that animal behavior is not based on derivation (استنباط) and analogy (قياس) but on divine inspiration (إلهام) and subjugation (تسخير), resulting in uniformity, unlike human creativity which is varied and reason-based.

Checkpoint
What is the principle of the human ability to devise wondrous crafts, according to this passage?
A) The body
B) The intellect
C) The imagination
D) The hands

Key Takeaway
Human inventiveness is rooted in rational imagination and bodily action, distinct from animal behaviors that are divinely inspired and uniform.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you develop a new skill or craft, do you consciously engage your rational imagination (khayāl) and derive through reasoning, or do you rely on habit and imitation like the animals? What would change if you deliberately used the human faculty of istinbāṭ?
?
Consider the uniformity of your daily religious practices. Are they driven by genuine rational understanding and personal engagement, or have they become mere routines inspired by external pressure? How can you re-awaken the derivation of worship from your own heart and mind?
?
The passage warns that animal behavior is uniform because it is from divine subjugation. Is there any area of your life—thoughts, actions, or beliefs—that is uniform and unquestioned because you have submitted to external control rather than exercising your God-given reason? What step can you take today to move from ‘taskhīr’ to ‘istinbāṭ’?
